< Text>
I've been a repeat customer of this joint about four times in the last two months.  Naturally, I have a few things to say.  First, one would think that the "all you can eat" would impact the quality of the individual servings.  One would be quite wrong. The quality of food is excellent.  I order a mix of nigiri and rolls.  You cannot hide bad fish on nigiri, and this fish is definitely fresh.   Also, the rolls are pretty big, and there are a large variety to shoose from.  Second, not only is the price super reasonable for sushi, but I really worry that it's too low to sustainably operate a business.  Lastly, a lot of the seating is made of super high booths.  The rest is normal casual fair.  Those booths are an excellent place to bring your friends and just hang out.  Isolated with great food.  I will definitely be returning.<//Text>

As always I choose Meiga fo the salmon. And I was not disapointed. The first round of 50 pieces were excellent. Nice thick slice, low rice ball, and the 2nd round cuts with the fatty bits, delicious. <userid>101893409950422050898<//userid>< user_name>
Thomas T</user_name>
<Time>1545598187414<//Time>< Rate>
5<//Rate>
<text>I have been there 5 or 6 times now. It has been consistently a good experience. Parking can be tough, but there is a parking structure, buses, and train nearby. This bar has a lot going on. The game area includes shuffleboard, pool, and darts. Smoking out front/back, well, you'll see. :)  The full bar has taps, wine, and a menu of mixed drinks (perfect for when I came in brain dead and didn't know what I wanted). It includes some creative and some times strong, good deals. The food has always been good and range from a small inexpensive cup of chili (perfect when needing a little something to eat when hammering back a few strong drinks) to elaborate more expensive options.  The walls have many flat tv screens, some of which are playing videos that I grew up with. There is also a juke box to play your own songs from your smartphone. <Text>Where to start with this review? The delicious wine? The friendly service that quickly makes you feel like family? The ridiculously fun wine pick up parties (well, pre-COVID at least)? Coomber is special. You walk in and are immediately greeted with a huge smile because the staff actually get to really know the regulars. The wine itself has a wide spectrum of varietals, prices, vintages, and "quality". I put that in quotes because it isn't necessarily the most expensive stuff that we actually enjoy the most. The Santa Maria Pinot Noir is fantastic and a great value. The chardonnays are all slightly different and would fall into that category as well. Regardless of whether to stop in for a glass (when it opens up for tastings instead of take out bottles) or become a wine club or locker member, give it a shot. You'll feel at home!< /Text><Pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipN94H8c601vs1LGyD9FeR-lkMCzG_Fu-wlMYblK=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPs4GW5WkL4s3ukSwB59a3YDhBiQ-vwdYfFKzMi=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]</Pics>< Resp>

<Text>Coomber Wines Tasting room is a great addition to downtown Oceanside. Coomber has an extensive selection of Whites and Reds. Our wine hosts were Ian and Megan, who were both very knowledgeable about the wines. Ian greeted us with a complimentary taste of their Rose, which is light and delicate. We opted for an All Red Tasting which consisted of 3 Pinot Noirs and 3 Cabernets. Like all good wine tastings they start out light and get progressively more robust. Ranging from the 2016 Vintner's Collection California Pinot Noir, which has a gorgeous bouquet and is light and playful to drink and the way up to the 2012 Private Reserve Rutherford Cabernet Sauvignon which is very earthy with big flavors that open up as you hold it in your mouth. I'd give them 0 stars if I could honestly. We purchased an air conditioner unit from them around 2011 with a warranty that extends into approximately 2022. First Arctic Air didn't install the unit correctly which cause water damage to our roof after some rainstorms passed by. After having people inspect the roof we had another local air conditioner company inspect the unit and tell Arctic Air how it was installed incorrectly. Later on after many complaints of one of our rooms not receiving enough cold air, Arctic Air thought it was a great idea to install a new vent that requires a filter 11 and 1/2 feet in the air on the roof of the tallest room in our house. However where the company really shined was this summer when the unit broke down. After waiting for hours for their serviceman to show up and take a look at the unit they informed us that the parts they needed were not available on weekends through our warranty and that we would either have to wait until the following Monday to get the parts through our warranty cause the place they get them from was already closed because it was Friday. However they "generously" offered to get the part for us the following morning if we paid them 350 dollars for it. We opted to get a second opinion on the unit after hearing the unfair price and ultimately decided to pay the 350. The next day they showed up, fixed the unit and charged us 750 dollars instead. Take my advice, don't call this company and forget they even exist. Take your money elsewhere.< /Text>

<user>110830390221669638642< /user><name>Christine Mamuad<//name>< date>
1614731853720< /date>
<Rating>4<//Rating>< Text>
Tarla boasts an extensive selection of food and drinks and a line of tables going down the sidewalk, but when we went for brunch at 12:30 on a Sunday, they were already out of two items that we wanted (octopus salad and fried calamari) and promptly ran out of the third (zucchini fritters) after we ordered (the table next to us tried and failed).

That said, we really enjoyed our food! The zucchini fritters were freshly made and delightful--if you're going to eat something fried, it might as well have some vegetable content. I thoroughly enjoyed my crab benedict with spinach, and my fiancee liked the beef and lamb gyro plate, despite the sting of disappointment over not having the octopus. The side potatoes were shockingly fantastic, well made and well seasoned. In a futile attempt to slow the expansion of my waistline, I usually try not to overload on carbs, but these potatoes were so good I just gave up and shoveled them in.

The Black Manhattan cocktail was decent, but I advise that you stay away from the Tarla Sangria. It was sadly diluted, and what little flavor could be detected was just not good. I couldn't finish even half of it.

Service was excellent, and we really appreciated our energetic and informative server, who did a great job despite having to run up and down the sidewalk to get to her tables.

Overall, this was a great spot for an outdoor Mediterranean brunch, provided you arrive early enough to order what you want before they run out!</Text>

<Review>Mm mm what a delish Mediterranean experience. We originally made ressies for 7pm on a Saturday after wine tasting, but need some extra rest before dinner, and they gladly moved out our ressie time to 8pm. As easily as they were able to accommodate, we were expecting a light crowd. But boy were we wrong. There were tons of outside seating, and about a dozen ppl waiting around to be seated.

There was a bit of disorganization as the hostesses scrambled to figure out where to seat ppl. They did, however, get us seated right away (after the 15mins it took to just check-in). The waiters constantly filled and refilled out water glasses, which was definitely needed after a long day of wine tasting!

We opted to get one main and more sides, since things were all sounding delish. While the truffle mushroom risotto sounded amazing, we opted to lean more on the Mediterranean inspired dishes - whole branzino, octopus salad, and meatballs. My buds didn‚Äôt go Mediterranean and tried the pasta and burger...which they both thought were meh. Fortunately for us, our dishes were spot on! Branzino was crispy on the outside, and buttery soft on the inside. As for the octopus salad, it was perfectly tender.

Tl;dr: check-in for free hummus. Order the inspired Mediterranean dishes! Make a ressie to skip the line!< /Review></record></dataset><record>

<Name>Maria Benavides</Name><Date>1615951097344</Date><Rating>5</Rating>< text>
My husband been Turkish, everytime we go to a Turkish restaurante in the US we don't have high expectations, after reading out Tarla description on their menu and how the restaurant prides on the origins of the ingredients, it did raised our expectations.

We order the dip trio, grilled octopus salad and meatballs, none of them disappointed us. I will recommend all of them but specially the octopus and meatballs.

The pomegranate cabernet short rib with risotto was really delicious.

My husband described their pistachio baklava as the best he has tried in the US!

They even have Turkish Raki, a nice environment and their staff is very good, Santiago took very good care of us. The owner and manager were also taking good care and walking around the tables asking if everything was good. It feel very personal.
Their price is very good and their portion sizes are very good.

My husband only disappointment was the absence of Turkish tea, we understand most of customers would not ask for it, however we will strongly suggest the establishment to offer complimentary Turkish tea to their customers pairing baklava, promoting the culture.

We are planning to come back tomorrow for their lentil soup. Please don't miss this place if you are in Napa< /text>

<Date>1531504789936</Date>< rating>

<Review>This is a late post, but I have returned to Napa after assisting with the Napa valley fires last October that ravaged the area and destroyed many homes. Eight of our firefighters from Washington state broke away for a dinner while on break from the fire lone and are at Tarla. What we experienced in the midst of a local disaster was amazing! While the food was expertly prepared and very delicious, what was even more amazing was the service and hospitality. Since we were in uniform, the head chef and owner had come out to our table and thanked us for coming to their hometown to help local responders. They then told us that the meal was going to be picked up by them with no charge to our party. This included complimentary appetizers that were brought to our table by a party eating at the bar and dessert offered by another resident of the area. What is so amazing is the generosity provided by those who were directly affected by the fires and one who had even lost her home. What a wonderful story, especially in the current climate in which we live. Thank you all and I will be visiting Tarla with my family to show appreciation to the staff today.</Review><Pics>None< /Pics>< resp>

< text>
We were in CA for the weekend and chose Tarla Mediterranean Restaurant because Mediterranean food just sounded good. We went early on a Saturday, and the place was empty. For the life of me, I cannot see why. It is a beautiful space, and everything about the meal was wonderful. We started with some Hummus, grilled thallium and the Brussels sprouts, and they were all absolutely fresh, excellently prepared and presented, and delicious. The three members of our party had Shish Kabob, Beef Sharma and the Sea Bass, and we were all much more than satisfied with our choices. The service was attentive without being overbearing, and the experience was wonderful from start to finish. I don't know why there wasn't a line out the door, as this restaurant deserves it.<//text>

<Date>1513839809728<//Date>< Review>
Went here for dinner after a day of wine tasting.

For a starter, we ordered the meze plate to split. To be honest, I was pretty underwhelmed with this. The hummus and baba ghanoush did not resemble the authentic versions of themselves, but the dolmas were pretty good.

However, this place did seriously redeem themselves with their drinks and entrees. My friend and I split the white truffle and mushroom risotto- which is literally HEAVEN! SO delicious, as well as the Pan Roasted Mediterranean Branzino Fish- which was equally delicious.

They were also very accommodating to my gluten free diet. Each of us ordered cocktails, and they were all phenomenal! Highly recommend the chambord margarita!< /Review>

<user_name>Thomas Kennelly</user_name><Time>1437108222618<//Time><rate>3< /rate>< Review>
We have been to Tarla several times and always enjoyed it, but tonight was a disappointment. The meze was delicious as always but the moussaka, previously delicious, was different this time -- a huge multilayered square hunk, overcooked, unattractive, with a little red sauce. None of the three who ordered it could eat more than half.A new chef perhaps?
The service was good but the restaurant, though not fully booked, was very noisy. And they seem to have raised their prices. The four of us had one meze plate, three moussakas, one eggplant, four coctails, and one bottle of wine ($31), -- no desserts or coffees - and the bill came to $187.00 before tip..We do not plan to return.</Review>

< text>
Food:
- Baba ganoush - nice and creamy with olive oil and parsley sprinkled on top; served with a nicely toasted pita
- Roast fish sandwich (bronzino) - fish is cooked to about medium with some parts being flaky and moist and other parts still raw.  It was pretty good, served with slaw and tzaziki sauce; Potatoes - lightly crisp chunks with paprika seasoning, and a side of spicy aioli for dipping
- Chicken kabob - one skewer with about 5 pieces, a bit dry. A pyramid of rice, soft and moist with some salt and chickpeas. The soup of the day was a slightly spicy tomato soup with some cheese on top

Service:
- good

Ambiance:
- large place, with outdoor seating
- nice, yet still casual< /text>
